## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Materials Science: Constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling stress as a function of strain and temperature, which is a common problem in constitutive modeling of materials. The goal is to describe how materials deform and respond to stress under various conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear Elasticity: sigma = E * epsilon (small deformations of linear materials)
- Viscoelasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon^(1/2) + c2 * exp(-c3 * t) (complexity in material response over time)
- Exponential Hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) (additional hardening as strain increases)
- Hyperelasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon^(c1) * (1 + c2 * epsilon^(c3)) (material stress based on strain energy density)
- Thermal Stress: sigma = alpha * epsilon * T (thermal expansion-induced stress)
- Thermoplasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T (stress relaxation over temperature)
- Thermomechanical coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T^(c2) (non-linear interaction between strain and temperature)
- Ductile failure: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon^(c3) (representing material failure through strain and stress)
- Viscoplasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 / (1 + c2 * epsilon^(c3)) (time-dependent material flow rule)
- Arrhenius-like kinetics: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (dependencies between stress and temperature in activated processes)
- Power-law creep: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 / T) (creep deformation controlled by stress and temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Stress-strain curve evolution → sigmoidal/rational fractions with exponent terms
- Thermal activation → exp terms with temperature as argument
- Material hardening → exponential/ polynomial expressions of strain
- Viscoelastic behavior → terms involving strain history and exponential decay
- Ductile failure → polynomial/multiple exponential expressions of strain and stress
- Thermomechanical coupling → interaction terms involving strain, temperature, and exponentials
- Linear/ non-linear material response → multiplicative expressions of strain and stress
- Temperature-dependent material properties → terms involving exp, log or rational functions of temperature
